# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Summary

I traced the complete call chain through Firefox's layout engine, identifying **22 key C++ source files** and **18 important symbols** that form the pipeline from CSS style changes to WebRender updates:

### The 5-Stage Chain:

1. **Style Change Notification** (`RestyleManager::PostRestyleEvent`)
   - Initial notification when CSS styles change
   - Notifies Servo style engine of hints

2. **Frame Style Recomputation** (`RestyleManager::ProcessRestyledFrames`)
   - Servo traversal recalculates styles
   - Generates change hints for affected frames

3. **Dirty-Frame Reflow Scheduling** (`PresShell::FrameNeedsReflow`)
   - Marks frames as dirty with proper bits
   - Schedules reflow for affected subtrees

4. **Display List Construction** (`nsLayoutUtils::PaintFrame` → `nsDisplayListBuilder`)
   - Recursively builds display list items
   - Uses retained display lists for optimization
   - Captures visual rendering order and clipping

5. **WebRender Layer Update** (`WebRenderLayerManager::EndTransactionWithoutLayer` → `WebRenderCommandBuilder::BuildWebRenderCommands`)
   - Converts display items to WebRender commands
   - Sends to compositor process via IPC
   - GPU renders and presents on screen

The answer file includes the complete call flow, architectural insights, and all relevant file paths and symbol names needed to understand this critical rendering pipeline.

traces how a CSS style change propagates through Firefox's layout engine to trigger display list construction and WebRender updates. This involves 5 major stages: style change notification, frame style recomputation, dirty-frame reflow scheduling, display list construction, and WebRender layer updates.\\n\\n### Stage 1: Style Change Notification\\n**File**: `layout/style/RestyleManager.cpp`\\n**Symbol**: `RestyleManager::PostRestyleEvent()`\\n\\nWhen CSS styles change (e.g., via JavaScript or stylesheet modifications), the `RestyleManager::PostRestyleEvent()` function is called. This function:\\n- Takes an Element, RestyleHint, and change hint\\n- Calls `Servo_NoteExplicitHints()` to notify the Servo style engine\\n- Records that non-animation restyles have occurred\\n- Increments the undisplayed restyle generation\\n\\nThe `RestyleManager` class (defined in `layout/style/RestyleManager.h`) manages all restyle operations for a given `nsPresContext` and coordinates with the `ServoStyleSet` to perform style computation.\\n\\n### Stage 2: Frame Style Recomputation\\n**Files**: \\n- `layout/style/ServoStyleSet.h/cpp`\\n- `layout/style/RestyleManager.cpp`\\n\\n**Symbols**: `ServoStyleSet`, `RestyleManager::ProcessRestyledFrames()`\\n\\nThe `ServoStyleSet` contains all style sheets and manages the Servo stylist. When styles need to be recomputed:\\n1. The Servo traversal performs style recalculation for affected elements\\n2. A `nsStyleChangeList` is generated containing the changed elements and their change hints\\n3. `RestyleManager::ProcessRestyledFrames()` processes this list, iterating through each changed frame and applying appropriate change hints\\n4. These change hints include `nsChangeHint_NeedReflow`, `nsChangeHint_RepaintFrame`, `nsChangeHint_ReconstructFrame`, etc.\\n\\n### Stage 3: Dirty-Frame Reflow Scheduling  \\n**File**: `layout/base/PresShell.cpp`\\n**Symbol**: `PresShell::FrameNeedsReflow()`\\n\\nWhen `ProcessRestyledFrames()` encounters a change hint that requires reflow:\\n1. It calls `PresShell::FrameNeedsReflow()` with the affected frame\\n2. This function marks the frame and its ancestors with dirty bits (`NS_FRAME_IS_DIRTY` or `NS_FRAME_HAS_DIRTY_CHILDREN`)\\n3. It clears intrinsic size caches and marks the frame as needing reflow\\n4. The dirty frames are added to `mDirtyRoots` for processing during the next reflow cycle\\n5. Eventually, `PresShell::DoFlushPendingNotifications()` initiates the actual reflow operation\\n\\n### Stage 4: Display List Construction\\n**Files**:\\n- `layout/base/nsLayoutUtils.cpp`\\n- `layout/painting/nsDisplayList.h/cpp`\\n- `layout/painting/RetainedDisplayListBuilder.h/cpp`\\n\\n**Symbols**: \\n- `nsLayoutUtils::PaintFrame()`\\n- `nsDisplayListBuilder`\\n- `RetainedDisplayListBuilder`\\n\\nDuring the paint phase:\\n1. `PresShell::PaintInternal()` initiates painting for a frame\\n2. It calls `nsLayoutUtils::PaintFrame()`, passing the frame and paint flags\\n3. `PaintFrame()` creates or retrieves a `RetainedDisplayListBuilder` (for retained display lists)\\n4. The builder's `nsDisplayListBuilder` then recursively traverses the frame tree\\n5. Each frame's `BuildDisplayList()` method is invoked to generate display items\\n6. The display items are organized into a hierarchical display list structure that captures the visual rendering order and clipping regions\\n\\n### Stage 5: WebRender Layer Update\\n**Files**:\\n- `gfx/layers/wr/WebRenderLayerManager.h/cpp`\\n- `gfx/layers/wr/WebRenderCommandBuilder.h/cpp`\\n- `gfx/layers/wr/WebRenderBridgeChild.h/cpp`\\n- `gfx/webrender_bindings/WebRenderAPI.h/cpp`\\n\\n**Symbols**:\\n- `WebRenderLayerManager::EndTransactionWithoutLayer()`\\n- `WebRenderCommandBuilder::BuildWebRenderCommands()`\\n- `WebRenderBridgeChild`\\n- `DisplayListBuilder` (WebRender's Rust builder)\\n\\nAfter display list construction:\\n1. `WebRenderLayerManager::EndTransactionWithoutLayer()` is called with the display list\\n2. The resulting WebRender display list is sent via `WebRenderBridgeChild` to the compositor process\\n4. The compositor renders the WebRender display list using the GPU and presents it on screen\\n\\n### Key Architectural Insights\\n\\n1. **Servo Integration**: Firefox uses Servo's style engine (via bindings in `layout/style/ServoStyleSet`) for CSS style computation, which is highly optimized for parallel traversal.\\n\\n2. **Change Hints**: The system uses fine-grained change hints to determine the minimal work needed - some changes only require repaints, others require reflows, and others require frame reconstruction.\\n\\n3. **Retained Display Lists**: Firefox uses retained display lists (managed by `RetainedDisplayListBuilder`) that can be incrementally updated based on which frames have actually changed, avoiding full rebuild.\\n\\n4. **WebRender Abstraction**: The `WebRenderLayerManager` abstracts WebRender details, translating Gecko's display list format into WebRender commands without tight coupling.\\n\\n5. **Asynchronous Rendering**: The WebRender bridge uses IPC to communicate with the compositor in a separate process, allowing non-blocking rendering.\\n\\n### Call Flow Summary\\n`PostRestyleEvent` \u2192 `ProcessRestyledFrames` \u2192 `FrameNeedsReflow` \u2192 `DoFlushPendingNotifications` \u2192 `PaintInternal` \u2192 `PaintFrame` \u2192 `nsDisplayListBuilder::BuildDisplayList` \u2192 `WebRenderLayerManager::EndTransactionWithoutLayer` \u2192 `WebRenderCommandBuilder::BuildWebRenderCommands` \u2192 Compositor rendering\"\n}\n",

traces how a CSS style change propagates through Firefox's layout engine to trigger display list construction and WebRender updates. This involves 5 major stages: style change notification, frame style recomputation, dirty-frame reflow scheduling, display list construction, and WebRender layer updates.\\n\\n### Stage 1: Style Change Notification\\n**File**: `layout/style/RestyleManager.cpp`\\n**Symbol**: `RestyleManager::PostRestyleEvent()`\\n\\nWhen CSS styles change (e.g., via JavaScript or stylesheet modifications), the `RestyleManager::PostRestyleEvent()` function is called. This function:\\n- Takes an Element, RestyleHint, and change hint\\n- Calls `Servo_NoteExplicitHints()` to notify the Servo style engine\\n- Records that non-animation restyles have occurred\\n- Increments the undisplayed restyle generation\\n\\nThe `RestyleManager` class (defined in `layout/style/RestyleManager.h`) manages all restyle operations for a given `nsPresContext` and coordinates with the `ServoStyleSet` to perform style computation.\\n\\n### Stage 2: Frame Style Recomputation\\n**Files**: \\n- `layout/style/ServoStyleSet.h/cpp`\\n- `layout/style/RestyleManager.cpp`\\n\\n**Symbols**: `ServoStyleSet`, `RestyleManager::ProcessRestyledFrames()`\\n\\nThe `ServoStyleSet` contains all style sheets and manages the Servo stylist. When styles need to be recomputed:\\n1. The Servo traversal performs style recalculation for affected elements\\n2. A `nsStyleChangeList` is generated containing the changed elements and their change hints\\n3. `RestyleManager::ProcessRestyledFrames()` processes this list, iterating through each changed frame and applying appropriate change hints\\n4. These change hints include `nsChangeHint_NeedReflow`, `nsChangeHint_RepaintFrame`, `nsChangeHint_ReconstructFrame`, etc.\\n\\n### Stage 3: Dirty-Frame Reflow Scheduling  \\n**File**: `layout/base/PresShell.cpp`\\n**Symbol**: `PresShell::FrameNeedsReflow()`\\n\\nWhen `ProcessRestyledFrames()` encounters a change hint that requires reflow:\\n1. It calls `PresShell::FrameNeedsReflow()` with the affected frame\\n2. This function marks the frame and its ancestors with dirty bits (`NS_FRAME_IS_DIRTY` or `NS_FRAME_HAS_DIRTY_CHILDREN`)\\n3. It clears intrinsic size caches and marks the frame as needing reflow\\n4. The dirty frames are added to `mDirtyRoots` for processing during the next reflow cycle\\n5. Eventually, `PresShell::DoFlushPendingNotifications()` initiates the actual reflow operation\\n\\n### Stage 4: Display List Construction\\n**Files**:\\n- `layout/base/nsLayoutUtils.cpp`\\n- `layout/painting/nsDisplayList.h/cpp`\\n- `layout/painting/RetainedDisplayListBuilder.h/cpp`\\n\\n**Symbols**: \\n- `nsLayoutUtils::PaintFrame()`\\n- `nsDisplayListBuilder`\\n- `RetainedDisplayListBuilder`\\n\\nDuring the paint phase:\\n1. `PresShell::PaintInternal()` initiates painting for a frame\\n2. It calls `nsLayoutUtils::PaintFrame()`, passing the frame and paint flags\\n3. `PaintFrame()` creates or retrieves a `RetainedDisplayListBuilder` (for retained display lists)\\n4. The builder's `nsDisplayListBuilder` then recursively traverses the frame tree\\n5. Each frame's `BuildDisplayList()` method is invoked to generate display items\\n6. The display items are organized into a hierarchical display list structure that captures the visual rendering order and clipping regions\\n\\n### Stage 5: WebRender Layer Update\\n**Files**:\\n- `gfx/layers/wr/WebRenderLayerManager.h/cpp`\\n- `gfx/layers/wr/WebRenderCommandBuilder.h/cpp`\\n- `gfx/layers/wr/WebRenderBridgeChild.h/cpp`\\n- `gfx/webrender_bindings/WebRenderAPI.h/cpp`\\n\\n**Symbols**:\\n- `WebRenderLayerManager::EndTransactionWithoutLayer()`\\n- `WebRenderCommandBuilder::BuildWebRenderCommands()`\\n- `WebRenderBridgeChild`\\n- `DisplayListBuilder` (WebRender's Rust builder)\\n\\nAfter display list construction:\\n1. `WebRenderLayerManager::EndTransactionWithoutLayer()` is called with the display list\\n2. This invokes `WebRenderCommandBuilder::BuildWebRenderCommands()` which:\\n   - Iterates through the display list items\\n   - Converts each display item into WebRender commands\\n   - Builds a `wr::DisplayListBuilder` (from the Rust WebRender library)\\n   - Manages clipping, transforms, and filter effects\\n   - Creates texture/image keys for images and async textures\\n3. The resulting WebRender display list is sent via `WebRenderBridgeChild` to the compositor process\\n4. The compositor renders the WebRender display list using the GPU and presents it on screen\\n\\n### Key Architectural Insights\\n\\n1. **Servo Integration**: Firefox uses Servo's style engine (via bindings in `layout/style/ServoStyleSet`) for CSS style computation, which is highly optimized for parallel traversal.\\n\\n2. **Change Hints**: The system uses fine-grained change hints to determine the minimal work needed - some changes only require repaints, others require reflows, and others require frame reconstruction.\\n\\n3. **Retained Display Lists**: Firefox uses retained display lists (managed by `RetainedDisplayListBuilder`) that can be incrementally updated based on which frames have actually changed, avoiding full rebuild.\\n\\n4. **WebRender Abstraction**: The `WebRenderLayerManager` abstracts WebRender details, translating Gecko's display list format into WebRender commands without tight coupling.\\n\\n5. **Asynchronous Rendering**: The WebRender bridge uses IPC to communicate with the compositor in a separate process, allowing non-blocking rendering.\\n\\n### Call Flow Summary\\n`PostRestyleEvent` \u2192 `ProcessRestyledFrames` \u2192 `FrameNeedsReflow` \u2192 `DoFlushPendingNotifications` \u2192 `PaintInternal` \u2192 `PaintFrame` \u2192 `nsDisplayListBuilder::BuildDisplayList` \u2192 `WebRenderLayerManager::EndTransactionWithoutLayer` \u2192 `WebRenderCommandBuilder::BuildWebRenderCommands` \u2192 Compositor rendering\"\n}\n",
